<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer14958407252229212349">Once an aristocrat in the heady days of pre-revolutionary France, now Lestat is a rockstar in the demonic, shimmering 1980s. He rushes through the centuries in search of others like him, seeking answers to the mystery of his terrifying exsitence. His story, the second volume in Anne Rice's best-selling Vampire Chronicles, is mesmerizing, passionate, and thrilling.</span>

      </div>
</div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_41564247">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/41564247" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1817719-eddie-black" class="left imgcol" title="Eddie Black"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1229726788p2/1817719.jpg" alt="Eddie Black" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/41564247?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 12, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1817719-eddie-black" class="user" title="Eddie Black">Eddie Black</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/43814.The_Vampire_Lestat" title="Paperback 9780345476883" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer41564247">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18226056520882311552">This is one of those books that defined me. I don't mean that I turned goth or vampire or whatever. No... it started me thinking.<br /><br />I was born and raised in the South. I didn't read anything else other than fantasy novels (like Dragonlance). I joined the Marines in 89 and while watching a movie about a teenage vampire it was mentioned that Dracula is 'good literature'. I went to the base library to check out Dracula and beside it on the shelf was this book. I took this one instead.<br /><br />The book was grea</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18226056520882311552">This is one of those books that defined me. I don't mean that I turned goth or vampire or whatever. No... it started me thinking.<br /><br />I was born and raised in the South. I didn't read anything else other than fantasy novels (like Dragonlance). I joined the Marines in 89 and while watching a movie about a teenage vampire it was mentioned that Dracula is 'good literature'. I went to the base library to check out Dracula and beside it on the shelf was this book. I took this one instead.<br /><br />The book was great. I loved it. The book engendered a question within me that never found any sunlight growing up a protestant in the Deep South. That queston, can something evil love? The values of the Southern protestant is one of black and white and there is no mixing, no grey, no overlap. By witnessing the drama of Lestat's journey, this manifestation of the Shadow declaring it's evil and it's good... I questioned this myself. <br /><br />It is a slippery slope to question everything. With no reading, history, or even exposure to any philosophy (Arkansas public school after all) I now asked questions about ethics, the nature of God, what is beauty, morality, and more. I had become a philosopher (though not a good one).<br /><br />Now, 17 years later I've been around the world many times, am nearing the completion of two degrees (psychology and philosophy) and am a much different, much broader, much more deepened soul. The questions I've asked, the roads I've taken, the experiences I've had, are all a result of my search for my own truth. A lot of that was set afire because of reading this book. <br /><br />I know that many bemoan Anne's move from the supernatural and to Christian writings. It's her life and I respect that. Yet I am reminded of something Jung said, we do not become enlighted by imagining beings of light, but by making the darkness visible (I'm paraphrasing). Lestat might not be a being of light (that's another topic) but his darkness is illuminating.<br /><br />This is one of my favorite books ever.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="18226056520882311552">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_79222311">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/79222311" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/266975-christine-ar" class="left imgcol" title="Christine (AR)"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1265493689p2/266975.jpg" alt="Christine (AR)" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/79222311?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 25, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/266975-christine-ar" class="user" title="Christine (AR)">Christine (AR)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/43814.The_Vampire_Lestat" title="Paperback 9780345476883" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/266975-christine-ar?shelf=sff" class="actionLinkLite">sff</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/266975-christine-ar?shelf=horror" class="actionLinkLite">horror</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/266975-christine-ar?shelf=urban_fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">urban_fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/266975-christine-ar?shelf=vampires" class="actionLinkLite">vampires</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer79222311">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17856665755917027540">Dear Anne Rice:<br /><br />NOT WORTHY.<br /><br />Signed, All Fictional Vampires Who Are Not Lestat<br /><br />This was a re-read for me, but in all honesty, I don't think I was ready for this book the first time I read it. Or at least, I didn't appreciate it for the sheer masterpiece of storytelling that it is, and it's not just the mood and the world and the mythology and the fast-moving plot -- more than anything, it's the characters. <br /><br />Lestat, of course, Rice's 'brat prince', arrogant and compassionate and impossible, all at the</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17856665755917027540">Dear Anne Rice:<br /><br />NOT WORTHY.<br /><br />Signed, All Fictional Vampires Who Are Not Lestat<br /><br />This was a re-read for me, but in all honesty, I don't think I was ready for this book the first time I read it. Or at least, I didn't appreciate it for the sheer masterpiece of storytelling that it is, and it's not just the mood and the world and the mythology and the fast-moving plot -- more than anything, it's the characters. <br /><br />Lestat, of course, Rice's 'brat prince', arrogant and compassionate and impossible, all at the same time -- he'd be enough to carry any book, imo, but the secondary characters are just as layered and bewitching, probably because we see them through Lestat's eyes. Nicki and his endless internal darkness; Armand, who manages to be both tragic and terrifying; Gabrielle, who seems like a force of nature; and even Louis, the whiny, unreliable narrator from <em>Interview</em> comes off as beautiful and mysterious, the star-crossed love of Lestat's afterlife. I swooned through the last chapter.<br /><br />I didn't care for the places Rice took this series after Queen of the Damned, but for me, Lestat continues to define the vampire-as-anti-hero genre. No other blood-sucker comes close. <br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17856665755917027540">...more</a>

          </span>

  <a href="/user/show/13636201-melissa" class="left imgcol" title="Melissa"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1451763872p2/13636201.jpg" alt="Melissa" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <a href="/user/show/13636201-melissa" class="user" title="Melissa">Melissa</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/43814.The_Vampire_Lestat" title="Paperback 9780345476883" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/13636201-melissa?shelf=all-time-favourites" class="actionLinkLite">all-time-favourites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/13636201-melissa?shelf=fantasy-paranormal-supernatural" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy-paranormal-supernatural</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/13636201-melissa?shelf=classics" class="actionLinkLite">classics</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer614165667">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1272460222140789920">Oh, how I love Anne Rice.<br />I actually started reading these books after I read Twilight. Yes, surprisingly, I went back to vampire fiction after that. Meyer is a good writer, but once you've met Anne's Vampires, you're never going back. Anyhow, this book was great. It still has the good kind of vampires: the ones that sleep in coffins, drink human blood and burn in the sunlight. <br /><br /><img width="240" height="192" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380421395i/836992.jpg" /><br /><br />This second book in the series wasn't disappointing, although I feared it might be, after reading the amazing 'Interview</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1272460222140789920">Oh, how I love Anne Rice.<br />I actually started reading these books after I read Twilight. Yes, surprisingly, I went back to vampire fiction after that. Meyer is a good writer, but once you've met Anne's Vampires, you're never going back. Anyhow, this book was great. It still has the good kind of vampires: the ones that sleep in coffins, drink human blood and burn in the sunlight. <br /><br /><img width="240" height="192" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380421395i/836992.jpg" /><br /><br />This second book in the series wasn't disappointing, although I feared it might be, after reading the amazing 'Interview With The Vampire'. It was also quite interesting, since I read this book after I'd seen the movie 'Queen of the Damned', which is based on this book and the next book. <br />The violin!! Turns out it didn't belong to a girl at all, but to Nicki, a boy. Damn you, untruthful modern cinema. <br /><br />The characters in this book were brilliant, the story-line was good and the ending was awesome. I can't wait to read 'The Queen of the Damned'. I own all of the books in this series and it's about time that I finish them all. Warning: Addicting series!</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_551693872">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/551693872" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3990525-crystal-starr-light" class="left imgcol" title="Crystal Starr Light"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1435785327p2/3990525.jpg" alt="Crystal Starr Light" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/551693872?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 19, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3990525-crystal-starr-light" class="user" title="Crystal Starr Light">Crystal Starr Light</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/16166538-the-vampire-lestat" title="Audiobook " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=simply-the-best" class="actionLinkLite">simply-the-best</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=horror" class="actionLinkLite">horror</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=so-good-it-s-awesome" class="actionLinkLite">so-good-it-s-awesome</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=audiobook" class="actionLinkLite">audiobook</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=in-tears-that-it-s-over" class="actionLinkLite">in-tears-that-it-s-over</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=characters-to-fall-in-love-with" class="actionLinkLite">characters-to-fall-in-love-with</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer551693872">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2347655967501120245">The year is 1984, and Lestat is the famous lead singer of the group, The Vampire Lestat. He stumbles upon a simple little book, "Interview with the Vampire", starring Louis, his ersatz lover of sorts (because vampires don't exactly have lovers the same way humans do). So Lestat sets the record straight and tells the tale of his life as a vampire.<br /><br />When people say this is better than <a title="Interview with the Vampire (Vampire Chronicles, #1) by Anne Rice" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43763.Interview_with_the_Vampire__Vampire_Chronicles___1_">Interview with the Vampire</a>, they are not kidding. This book is light years better than "Interview". I almost wish th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2347655967501120245">The year is 1984, and Lestat is the famous lead singer of the group, The Vampire Lestat. He stumbles upon a simple little book, "Interview with the Vampire", starring Louis, his ersatz lover of sorts (because vampires don't exactly have lovers the same way humans do). So Lestat sets the record straight and tells the tale of his life as a vampire.<br /><br />When people say this is better than <a title="Interview with the Vampire (Vampire Chronicles, #1) by Anne Rice" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43763.Interview_with_the_Vampire__Vampire_Chronicles___1_">Interview with the Vampire</a>, they are not kidding. This book is light years better than "Interview". I almost wish this book never ended, it was so good. I already have book 3 lined up to read - and normally, I would give myself a break, just so I didn't burn out.<br /><br />What makes "The Vampire Lestat" so good? Just about everything - from characters, to setting, to writing, to mythos. About the only thing I can critique is that at one point, not long after Gabrielle is turned and we meet Armand, the story kinda stalls and gets a bit dull. Oh, and when Marius is telling his story, I kinda got confused and thought we went back to Lestat's POV. But honestly, those are nitpicks - I enjoyed myself thoroughly with this book.<br /><br />Lestat is a WAY better protagonist than Louis. He's not so whiny, so pathetic, so useless. He's a master of his own life - sure, he contemplates whether he is evil and tends to choose victims who are evil (those women Louis says Lestat seduces? They are prostitutes that cheat sailors and probably kill them). He is a passionate being - he cares enormously for Nikola and Louis (some of the sweetest interactions in the book) and his mother (though his love for her gets a bit creepy in the "I don't think we should be kissing our MOM this way"). He is a curious being - he searches all over the Mediterranean for Marius and the source of answers. He is a powerful being - his powers attract the attention of Armand and Marius and when others can't stand being a vampire, he is able to press on.<br /><br />The rest of the cast is beautifully done as well. Gabrielle, Nikola, Marius, Armand, and even Louis all get dimension. They are real people, with real desires - Gabrielle to be set loose to live alone. Nikola to balance his "wicked" pursuit of the theater with his religious beliefs. And so on. And so forth.<br /><br />The story was engaging and exciting. I was enthralled with the depths of the mythos, a perfect balance of complex and yet simple - not a list of rules sloppily tacked together when the author needs to add a new challenge to her characters, but actual rules that make sense in the world and seem to originate naturally from the circumstances. And the addition of Akasha and her brother - I can't tell you how deliciously creeped out I was! I loved it!<br /><br />At this point, I'm just gushing. Honestly, I really loved this book and am SO GLAD I didn't give up on this series. If you like your vampires wicked and blood-thirsty, you definitely need to check out this series!!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2347655967501120245">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_264914337">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/264914337" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5105002-peter" class="left imgcol" title="Peter"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1448640054p2/5105002.jpg" alt="Peter" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/264914337?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 16, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5105002-peter" class="user" title="Peter">Peter</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/9727878-the-vampire-lestat" title="ebook 9780307575937" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5105002-peter?shelf=gothic" class="actionLinkLite">gothic</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5105002-peter?shelf=read-2012" class="actionLinkLite">read-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer264914337">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9259879391414942553">This was the Audible audio book, unabridged, read by Simon Vance. Who gives a really good performance, I love his vampire voice!<br /><br />Lestat de Lion court rises from his long hibernation in 1980 and decides to become a rockstar. He puts out an album and to accompany this he writes his autobiography - revealing the story of his youth as well as the history of the race of vampires, which started 4000 years ago in Ancient Egypt.<br /><br />Some gleaned facts: Anne Rice loves the words: 'preternatural' and 'savage ga</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9259879391414942553">This was the Audible audio book, unabridged, read by Simon Vance. Who gives a really good performance, I love his vampire voice!<br /><br />Lestat de Lion court rises from his long hibernation in 1980 and decides to become a rockstar. He puts out an album and to accompany this he writes his autobiography - revealing the story of his youth as well as the history of the race of vampires, which started 4000 years ago in Ancient Egypt.<br /><br />Some gleaned facts: Anne Rice loves the words: 'preternatural' and 'savage garden'. This is the band Savage Garden's favourite book (I imagine). <br /><br />Although it has a lot of similar themes, I did not enjoy this book as much as "Interview with a Vampire" for a number of reasons. I think because the plot is much more meandering and fragmented. It takes in four narrators - Lestat, Armand, Marius and another narrator in Ancient Egypt - and a lot of different geographic and cultural settings which I don't think Anne Rice captures quite as well as she does New Orleans or Paris.<br /><br />Some Spoilers...<br /><br />Rice has softened and rounded Lestat to make him more likeable compared to the evil, mysterious enigma of Interview. As a narrator he is a totally believable character (this is Rice's main strength) though I do not think his obsessions are as interesting as Louis'. He is a bit too confident and self assured. Gabrielle too was similar to Claudia, but again not quite as interesting, her concern that she will never change is represented by the fact she can never cut her hair, a brilliant weird sequence, but not nearly as strong as the stories spun around Claudia - the little girl who never grows old. Nicky, the other main character, was an entirely tedious and forgettable cypher. <br /><br />In terms of the story I loved the opening and the end and a lot of the sequences in Paris, but a lot of the stuff in Ancient Egypt - the history of the vampires etc – I found rather boring. I hated the development that now all the vampires can read minds, it just meant the prose drifted off into even more internal stuff than before. I hated that there was no big deaths - like in Interview. Nicky is the only character who dies and this isn't even 'onscreen' Lestat is informed of it in a letter, this is such a throwaway of good drama I can only assume that it was a lie and done so he can show up again sometime. Also, Lestat and Gabrielle miss the French Revolution because they are basically on holiday in Egypt, talk about throwing away more great dramatic opportunity. Anyway, if Queen of the Damned is set in the modern day I probably will end up reading it as, from the ending of this one, that seemed an interesting premise.<br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9259879391414942553">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_129596774">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/129596774" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1099002-kelly" class="left imgcol" title="Kelly"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1339718566p2/1099002.jpg" alt="Kelly" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/129596774?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 06, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1099002-kelly" class="user" title="Kelly">Kelly</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/396356.The_Vampire_Lestat" title="Paperback 9780345419644" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer129596774">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11118831575876220850">It is my suggestion that, if you want to sample Anne Rice, and have never read any of her other works, this may be the book you want to read instead of her most famous novel, "Interview with a Vampire." let me explain.<br />"The Vampire Lestat" is quite a different novel from the first in the series, because we are dealing with an entirely different vampire than the depressed and vulnerable Louis from Rice's first book. Don't get me wrong, Lestat was the antagonist in Interview but towards the end of</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11118831575876220850">It is my suggestion that, if you want to sample Anne Rice, and have never read any of her other works, this may be the book you want to read instead of her most famous novel, "Interview with a Vampire." let me explain.<br />"The Vampire Lestat" is quite a different novel from the first in the series, because we are dealing with an entirely different vampire than the depressed and vulnerable Louis from Rice's first book. Don't get me wrong, Lestat was the antagonist in Interview but towards the end of the novel you start to think maybe that's not the case. That single thought pushed me to read his story to find out why Lestat was the way he was.<br /><br />I LOVED learning about where Lestat came from and also finding out about ALL of the ancient vampires, all the way back to the very FIRST vampire. In Lestat's story, the reader goes throughout the centuries, as he meets other vampire's who tell their tales. This book feels like a world tour that goes back to Ancient Egyptian times, to classical Rome, to pagan Europe, to the times of the French Revolution, to an old, decaying (slightly creepy I might add) Parisian cemetery and back up to the present time. It was FUN to follow Lestats journey to find the truth..the same truth that Louis was always searching for, but never found. <br /><br />The entire story is fascinating and spans centuries as Lestat grows from a fledgling vampire into the emotional, lonely, angry, and finally carefree vampire he is upon setting foot on a San Francisco stage to perform his first rock concert in front of 15,000 screaming fans. (Yes, Lestat is a Rock star in the 1980's in this book! My first thought to that was, "Whatever!" But then it made sense.)<br /><br />Lestat now gets a chance to tell his OWN story, and it makes us (the reader) realize that he has suffered even more than Louis and shows that he is not a villain; he is the tragic hero of sorts. He is actually far more aware than Louis, something else that Louis doesn't see either. He is a gentle, innocent, thoughtful young man who has suffered so much in his life, and then he is forced into becoming one of the living dead, who now must kill to survive. It is explained to us why Lestat is the way he is and why he does the things he does which is truly interesting.<br /><br />When you read "Interview with a Vampire" you don't know then that Lestat is misunderstood by Louis, and therefore misunderstood by the reader, whom is seeing the story through Louis' eyes. The glimpses of Lestat we have in Interview with the Vampire, of his relationship with his father, of the way he acts, of his charm that Louis finds both attractive and repulsive, of his love of bright artificial light and his desire to live luxuriously, of his friendship with a young musician, of his doting upon Claudia and showering her with gifts, of his fear to lose Louis, of him emotionally distraught and pleading with Louis to come back to him in Paris (which I didn't understand at the time), and finally of the frail, broken, and pitiful shadow of a man he has become by the end of Louis's story, where Louis finds him again in New Orleans. All of these things are hints at the depth and complexity of the character of Lestat. <br /><br />In The Vampire Lestat, you will finally see the entire picture, and see the masterpiece of a character that Lestat is. The depth and the multi-dimensionality, and the humanity of Lestat. If you liked Louis before, you will still like him. But you will like Lestat even more because you will see how completely misunderstood he is and learn the story of the pain and sorrow he kept hidden in his heart, hidden underneath that charming facade that Louis encountered on his plantation in 1791. You will start to understand HOW Lestat could act the way he did towards Louis and Claudia which was the answer to the questions I was seeking in this book so I closed the covers of this book satisfied.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11118831575876220850">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_224271975">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/224271975" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5666413-erika" class="left imgcol" title="Erika"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1361128945p2/5666413.jpg" alt="Erika" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/224271975?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 20, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5666413-erika" class="user" title="Erika">Erika</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/43814.The_Vampire_Lestat" title="Paperback 9780345476883" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5666413-erika?shelf=series-following" class="actionLinkLite">series-following</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5666413-erika?shelf=horror" class="actionLinkLite">horror</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5666413-erika?shelf=supernatural" class="actionLinkLite">supernatural</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5666413-erika?shelf=adult" class="actionLinkLite">adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer224271975">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer522360838598855526"><em> <strong>Oh Lestat de Lioncourt, how can you be this rebel, <br />how dare you create such trouble while not giving a single thought to your actions.</strong> </em><br /><br />This is the second book on The Vampire Chronicles, and it is time for Lestat to tell his story. It starts in the year 1984 if my mind is not playing tricks on me, <br /><br /><em>(wow, i just realized that i was reading this book at the same time with the book <a title="1984 by George Orwell" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5470.1984">1984</a>. Isn't that weird? book set in 1984 while i was reading 1984... no?... but... are you sure?... not even a little?.</em></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText522360838598855526"><em>
  <strong>Oh Lestat de Lioncourt, how can you be this rebel, <br />how dare you create such trouble while not giving a single thought to your actions.</strong>
</em><br /><br />This is the second book on The Vampire Chronicles, and it is time for Lestat to tell his story. It starts in the year 1984 if my mind is not playing tricks on me, <br /><br /><em>(wow, i just realized that i was reading this book at the same time with the book <a title="1984 by George Orwell" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5470.1984">1984</a>. Isn't that weird? book set in 1984 while i was reading 1984... no?... but... are you sure?... not even a little?... well i... whatever, i think it's interesting :P)</em><br /><br />and Lestat has become a rockstar in a band called precisely <em>"The Vampire Lestat"</em>. This idea of a vampire becoming a rockstar seems a bit ridiculous to me at the beginning because during all the time in <a title="Interview with the Vampire (The Vampire Chronicles, #1) by Anne Rice" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43763.Interview_with_the_Vampire__The_Vampire_Chronicles___1_">Interview with the Vampire</a> they were saying Lestat was very handsome and crazy, so to define him later as an actual rockstar seemed a bit of a tool to trick people into thinking he's way cooler than he actually is, it didn't seem like a good idea to me.<br /><br />I couldn't help but imagine him on stage playing guitar and being stalked by millions of fans while, in his nature, he's supposed to be killing to feed, not just being cool and famous and... rockstar... (at this point it wouldn't have surprise me if he started to "sparkle" :S) And he actually sings, he goes onstage and starts singing things like <em>"I'm a vampire, and I'll suck your blood"</em> and other things.<br /><br />So I didn't like that, but luckily this didn't appear much in the book because for almost the entirety of the book Lestat was writing his story. Basically after the interview with Louis, the boy interviewer published the interview as a book which became a best seller, but everybody thought it was a work of fiction not a real thing. <br /><br />Lestat came across this book when he met the guys of the band and wanted to join them, he went to them and told them he was Lestat and got very surprised to realize that they already knew his name. They thought it was really awesome that he came to them and told them he was Lestat from the book interview instead of other famous vampires like Dracula for example. So He read greedily the book and thought he needed to tell his own story, so he typed it all from the beginning when he was turned into one of the damned creatures.<br /><br />His story was really interesting, it covered way too many details of many things, hence the book is long. I really liked especially when other vampires told him a bit of their back story, more specifically Marius. <br /><br />Marius is a very old vampire, he is the vampire who created Armand, and his story is so damn interesting, i wish i could read more about him. Since he is a very old vampire, his beginnings come from a very old age and you see historical facts here of ancient history, it's really fantastic!! All the chapters about Marius are my favorite parts of the book. <br /><br />In this part he also covered the way vampires started to exist in this world, Marius was not one of the first vampires but he sure knows which 2 were the first ones to appear and they are called The Father and The Mother. <strong>Oh, i so enjoyed this part of the story, the whole book was worth it just for this part!</strong><br /><br />I also like so much all the philosophy it contains about death, life, existence, love, immortality, etc. Anne Rice is a great author, her prose is gorgeous, the descriptions are beautiful, but i can't bring myself to really love her books, sometimes i feel like they drag way too much and i feel the pace so slow and that makes me stop enjoying the story for a greater part of the book.<br /><br />At the ending <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[ Lestat gets in trouble because he published that book revealing all the secrets of the vampires, names, locations, everything and he's there being a rockstar, exposed to the world without keeping any secrets nor respecting vampire rules. And he's brought great danger over himself and those he loves.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and that leaves you in a sort of cliffhanger. SOOOO, we're in for great adventure for the next book, <a title="The Queen of the Damned (The Vampire Chronicles, #3) by Anne Rice" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43758.The_Queen_of_the_Damned__The_Vampire_Chronicles___3_">The Queen of the Damned</a>, apparently.<!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="522360838598855526">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_20985129">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/20985129" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/210421-bart" class="left imgcol" title="Bart"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1432909313p2/210421.jpg" alt="Bart" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/20985129?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 23, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/210421-bart" class="user" title="Bart">Bart</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/43814.The_Vampire_Lestat" title="Paperback 9780345476883" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Readers in general</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Bart by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/242534-todd">Todd</a>
  </div>



    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer20985129">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12213222304663044126">A happy surprise indeed. Perhaps it was a result of low expectations or a prior experience with the movie "Interview with the Vampire" that had me so unprepared to enjoy this novel.<br /><br /><em>The Vampire Lestat</em> is a great read. It may not have all the literary quality of, say, Cormac McCarthy's equally gruesome accounts, but it is more enjoyable on its first reading.<br /><br />What makes authors great, of course, is how their works hold up on revisits. Knowing the plotting and the conclusion of Anne Rice's novel, I'm</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12213222304663044126">A happy surprise indeed. Perhaps it was a result of low expectations or a prior experience with the movie "Interview with the Vampire" that had me so unprepared to enjoy this novel.<br /><br /><em>The Vampire Lestat</em> is a great read. It may not have all the literary quality of, say, Cormac McCarthy's equally gruesome accounts, but it is more enjoyable on its first reading.<br /><br />What makes authors great, of course, is how their works hold up on revisits. Knowing the plotting and the conclusion of Anne Rice's novel, I'm unlikely to go back to it. But let that dissuade no one from giving this novel a first reading.<br /><br />If there are shortcomings in this book, they derive from Rice's tries at ontological philosophy. She's brave to consider questions of immortality, of course, but probably not as wise to record her thoughts. In the first third, she tries to tackle immortality - and how it relates, ultimately, to good and evil - but she sort of loses her way. She has her characters who, for being inexperienced at being immortal, haven't the depth for it, making soliloquies about its consequences.<br /><br />Later on, though, when she comes to characters that are millennia old, she knows better and concedes the impenetrability of their plight. And along the way, she also kills off about 100 "immortals". This also seems to suggest that maybe all those pages of contemplating immortality should have remained behind in the novel's first draft.<br /><br />Otherwise, the book is a joy to read. It's lively and well written. For the most part, Rice moves the book at the right pace and proves, once more, that descriptive writing works great when it enhances the plot. Too many inexperienced writers seem to mistake descriptive writing <em>for</em> the plot. All such readers would be encouraged to review the last 15 pages of <em>The Vampire Lestat</em>; after 600 pages, Rice knows when to go full bore into description and make her novel's conclusion memorable.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12213222304663044126">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16761636174968798486">4.0 to 4.5 stars. Anne Rice's re-imagining of the "vampire" mythos is excellent and Lestat is on my list of "All Time Favorite" characters. As good as this novel is, the books that follow:<a title="The Queen of the Damned (The Vampire Chronicles, #3) by Anne Rice" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43758.The_Queen_of_the_Damned__The_Vampire_Chronicles___3_">The Queen of the Damned</a>, <a title="The Tale of the Body Thief (The Vampire Chronicles, #4) by Anne Rice" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/31336.The_Tale_of_the_Body_Thief__The_Vampire_Chronicles___4_">The Tale of the Body Thief</a> and <a title="Memnoch the Devil (The Vampire Chronicles, #5) by Anne Rice" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/31338.Memnoch_the_Devil__The_Vampire_Chronicles___5_">Memnoch the Devil</a> are even better. Highly Recommended? <br /><br />Nominee: World Fantasy Award for Best Novel (1986)<br />Nominee: Locus Award for Best Fantasy Novel (1986)</span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1114186762">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12556445909464787001">Anne Rice is definitely one of my favorite authors but as I said in my review for "Interview with the Vampire", in my opinion, Vampire Chronicles saga is divided into two parts; Interview with the Vampire and the rest of the books, especially by the shift in their point of view: the first point of view lies on Louis while in second lies on Lestat. That makes the "Vampire Lestat" and subsequent novels a more passionate and less melancholic mood than Interview with the vampire. Rice plunges us int</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12556445909464787001">Anne Rice is definitely one of my favorite authors but as I said in my review for "Interview with the Vampire", in my opinion, Vampire Chronicles saga is divided into two parts; Interview with the Vampire and the rest of the books, especially by the shift in their point of view: the first point of view lies on Louis while in second lies on Lestat. That makes the "Vampire Lestat" and subsequent novels a more passionate and less melancholic mood than Interview with the vampire. Rice plunges us into the world where light and darkness fight constantly between what's good or evil, what's ethical or unethical. It's a great novel, much more exciting than "Interview with the Vampire" and is ideal for all those fans of the vampire myth and good writing.<br /><br />Spanish version: <br />Anne Rice es sin duda una de mis autoras favoritas pero como ya dije mi crítica para "Entrevista con el Vampiro", en mi opinión la saga de crónicas vampíricas se divide en dos partes; entrevista con el vampiro y el resto de libros, sobre todo por el evidente cambio en el punto de vista, en la primera el punto de vista recae en Louis mientras que en la segunda en Lestat. Eso hace que a Lestat el vampiro y las siguientes novelas tengan un tinte algo más apasionado y mucho menos melancolico. Rice nos sumerge en un mundo en el que la luz y la oscuridad luchan constantemente en un discurso entre el bien y el mal, lo ético y lo perverso. Es una novela genial, mucho más trepidante que "entrevista con el vampiro" y es ideal para todos aquellos fans del mito y de la buena escritura. <br /></span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/753983-michelle?shelf=reviewed" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer414455256">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5456205339245656938">TL;DR - it's worth reading if you enjoy the franchise, the characters, and are willing to self-edit (that is, skip the repetitive expositions).<br /><br />Although I read this book when it was first published, and reread it a time or two in the intervening decades, most recently I "read" this book as an audio book, which is an interesting test for a book. The book is in the first person, so listening to it heightens the effect of Lestat telling you his story; however, I hadn't realized how much of the ponti</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5456205339245656938">TL;DR - it's worth reading if you enjoy the franchise, the characters, and are willing to self-edit (that is, skip the repetitive expositions).<br /><br />Although I read this book when it was first published, and reread it a time or two in the intervening decades, most recently I "read" this book as an audio book, which is an interesting test for a book. The book is in the first person, so listening to it heightens the effect of Lestat telling you his story; however, I hadn't realized how much of the pontificating I usually skipped over when rereading the book in print. At times during the narration I wanted to stop Lestat and tell him, "I get it--you've made your point. Move along, please." I had forgotten the endless exposition about the nature of good and evil and spirituality, and I had forgotten how much Lestat verges on being a "Mary Sue" (an overly idealized character). His flaws are extensive, some of which even acknowledged in faux-self-deprecation, but somehow everyone loves him despite these flaws, and forgives him the most outrageous transgressions, which always end up benefitting him.<br /><br />The character of Gabrielle has always been more interesting to me than Lestat. Where his extreme extraversion annoys me, her uncompromising introversion attracts. Where Lestat's transformation to vampire leads him to endless ruminations about the need to love humans and humanity, his dependence on and need of them, the utter lack of meaning in a life without the love of humans, Gabrielle uses her transformation to free her at last from the demands and needs of others. She sticks around for a few transitional decades to try to wean her son into adult independence, but ultimately puts her own selfhood first. <br /><br />Detaching to look at the structure of the book, the tale within a tale is carried too far, and by the time Lestat meets up with Marius, I was snorting as I counted the layers, as we have Lestat, who tells us the tale of himself listening to Marius, as Marius relates the tale of Marius listening to the tale of the Egyptian priest, who relates the story of Those Who Must Be Kept. There may have been another layer in there, but who can keep track? While the individual embedded stories were interesting, they also felt like a massive info dump, to give us the necessary background to appreciate the amazing specialness of Lestat, when he is the one to whom the Queen (silent and unmoving for centuries) responds.<br /><br />If you're going to read this book for the first time, make sure you have the next book "Queen of the Damned" ready, as "The Vampire Lestat" ends in a cliffhanger. <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5456205339245656938">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_473566477">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/473566477" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3031346-rebecca" class="left imgcol" title="Rebecca"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1266730996p2/3031346.jpg" alt="Rebecca" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/473566477?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 14, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3031346-rebecca" class="user" title="Rebecca">Rebecca</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/43814.The_Vampire_Lestat" title="Paperback 9780345476883" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3031346-rebecca?shelf=annoyed-me" class="actionLinkLite">annoyed-me</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3031346-rebecca?shelf=horror" class="actionLinkLite">horror</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3031346-rebecca?shelf=boring" class="actionLinkLite">boring</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3031346-rebecca?shelf=terrible" class="actionLinkLite">terrible</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3031346-rebecca?shelf=vampires" class="actionLinkLite">vampires</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer473566477">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16560765249273192118">You'll notice this took me well over a month to read, which should say all that needs to be said considering how much time I have to read at the moment and how fast I normally read books.<br /><br />That was going to be my entire review, until I came across this little gem of a line while powering through trying to finish yesterday: (said by Marius to Lestat) "The truth is most women are weak, be they mortal or immortal. But when they are strong, they are absolutely unpredictable" (page 409 in my edition).</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16560765249273192118">You'll notice this took me well over a month to read, which should say all that needs to be said considering how much time I have to read at the moment and how fast I normally read books.<br /><br />That was going to be my entire review, until I came across this little gem of a line while powering through trying to finish yesterday: (said by Marius to Lestat) "The truth is most women are weak, be they mortal or immortal. But when they are strong, they are absolutely unpredictable" (page 409 in my edition). My reaction was, what is that supposed to mean? Marius is, as far as I can tell, supposed to be a positive character, and this statement slips in without any further development (and because most ideas get pages and pages of lengthy consideration, I don't think it's wrong to call this out). I'd already taken issue with the (very few) women in Rice's book, so can't say I was terrible surprised. Furthermore, most of the female characters, who I guess would be considered "strong," are unpredictable - Claudia (from the previous book), Gabrielle, Akasha. It's not that being unpredictable is bad, it's just that this whole statement perpetuates out-dated views on women, that we're either weak, or prone to bouts of hysteria. Added to this were some weird and uncomfortable statements about the Western versus the Eastern world, in which the West is clearly better and more civilized. I would have stopped reading here if I hadn't set my mind on finishing it just to say I had.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_72098592">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/72098592" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/455717-jon-michael" class="left imgcol" title="Jon-michael"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1269899615p2/455717.jpg" alt="Jon-michael" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/72098592?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 22, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/455717-jon-michael" class="user" title="Jon-michael">Jon-michael</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/43814.The_Vampire_Lestat" title="Paperback 9780345476883" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer72098592">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17687755479859919377">This is one of those books that defined me. I do mean that I turned goth or vampire or whatever. No... it started me thinking.<br /><br />I was born and raised in the South. I didn't read anything else other than fantasy novels (like Dragonlance). I joined the Marines in 89 and while watching a movie about a teenage vampire it was mentioned that Dracula is 'good literature'. I went to the base library to check out Dracula and beside it on the shelf was this book. I took this one instead.<br /><br />The book was great.</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17687755479859919377">This is one of those books that defined me. I do mean that I turned goth or vampire or whatever. No... it started me thinking.<br /><br />I was born and raised in the South. I didn't read anything else other than fantasy novels (like Dragonlance). I joined the Marines in 89 and while watching a movie about a teenage vampire it was mentioned that Dracula is 'good literature'. I went to the base library to check out Dracula and beside it on the shelf was this book. I took this one instead.<br /><br />The book was great. I loved it. The book engendered a question within me that never found any sunlight growing up a protestant in the Deep South. That queston, can something evil love? The values of the Southern protestant is one of black and white and there is no mixing, no grey, no overlap. By witnessing the drama of Lestat's journey, this manifestation of the Shadow declaring it's evil and it's good... I questioned this myself.<br /><br />It is a slippery slope to question everything. With no reading, history, or even exposure to any philosophy (Arkansas public school after all) I now asked questions about ethics, the nature of God, what is beauty, morality, and more. I had become a philosopher (though not a good one).<br /><br />Now, 17 years later I've been around the world many times, am nearing the completion of two degrees (psychology and philosophy) and am a much different, much broader, much more deepened soul. The questions I've asked, the roads I've taken, the experiences I've had, are all a result of my search for my own truth. A lot of that was set afire because of reading this book.<br /><br />I know that many bemoan Anne's move from the supernatural and to Christian writings. It's her life and I respect that. Yet I am reminded of something Jung said, we do not become enlighted by imagining beings of light, but by making the darkness visible (I'm paraphrasing). Lestat might not be a being of light (that's another topic) but his darkness is illuminating.<br /><br />This is one of my favorite books ever.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17687755479859919377">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9779833530282022548">In "Interview With a Vampire", Lestat was the villain, and could be viewed as a cold, unfeeling monster. In the sequel, Lestat gets a chance to 'set the record straight.' Reading HIS account on his life, and the years spent with Louis, he actually manages to gain sympathy, and he fully admits to being a brat prince of the undead, and you fall in love with this vampire who listens to Beethoven while riding a motorcycle down the moonlit streets. Lestat has an ego so large, it is little wonder that</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9779833530282022548">In "Interview With a Vampire", Lestat was the villain, and could be viewed as a cold, unfeeling monster. In the sequel, Lestat gets a chance to 'set the record straight.' Reading HIS account on his life, and the years spent with Louis, he actually manages to gain sympathy, and he fully admits to being a brat prince of the undead, and you fall in love with this vampire who listens to Beethoven while riding a motorcycle down the moonlit streets. Lestat has an ego so large, it is little wonder that he chooses to become a rock star and write a book accounting his long life story, because where else can you find that level of admiration and worship if not from center stage, with a microphone, in front of thousands of people cheering you on like at a concert? Who else would write the book but Lestat himself? (Under the alias of Anne Rice, of course.) He proves to be so entertaining that all of the vampire books after that are told from his point of view.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_39675792">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/39675792" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1752489-cecilia" class="left imgcol" title="Cecilia"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1239838411p2/1752489.jpg" alt="Cecilia" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/39675792?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 09, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1752489-cecilia" class="user" title="Cecilia">Cecilia</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/63258.Lestat_el_Vampiro" title="Paperback 9788466616881" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">vampire lovers</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1752489-cecilia?shelf=anne-rice" class="actionLinkLite">anne-rice</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1752489-cecilia?shelf=vampires" class="actionLinkLite">vampires</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a onclick="Effect.toggle('reviewTextContainer39675792'); return false;" href="#">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer39675792">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17711488072560428022">Lestat... ¿qué se puede decir de un personaje tan seguro de si mismo, capaz de crueldades impensables, y a la vez, dueño de una personalidad terca, posesiva, egoista?<br />La historia de Lestat debería ser triste: un hombre joven, obligado a ser vampiro por un creador macabro y suicida. Pero no, su personalidad hace que acepte su nuevo estado como una forma más de sobrevivir en una París que nos resulta ajena, pero no extraña. <br />Es un vampiro que no se esconde, y que no acepta su destino de "condenado"</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17711488072560428022">Lestat... ¿qué se puede decir de un personaje tan seguro de si mismo, capaz de crueldades impensables, y a la vez, dueño de una personalidad terca, posesiva, egoista?<br />La historia de Lestat debería ser triste: un hombre joven, obligado a ser vampiro por un creador macabro y suicida. Pero no, su personalidad hace que acepte su nuevo estado como una forma más de sobrevivir en una París que nos resulta ajena, pero no extraña. <br />Es un vampiro que no se esconde, y que no acepta su destino de "condenado" ni siquiera cuando Armand y los suyos se lo hacen ver (particularmente, me encantó la vampira vieja y algo loca que estaba con el grupo). <br />Un dato curioso es que el cimetière des inocents sí existió en París, lamentablemente, fue uno de los tantos que se removieron en pos del crecimiento de la ciudad, pero algunos de sus nichos se encuentran bajo el suelo de París, en las cloacas. Lo sé por que quedé tan fascinada con Armand y los suyos que decidí rastrear el cementerio y encontré un libro al respecto. Más tarde, vi un documental, creo que del Discovery Channel o del History Channel, ya no recuerdo.<br />La vida itinerante y solitaria (por momentos) de Lestat no deja de sorprender, desde las noches compartidas con su madre, hasta la búsqueda incansable de Marius, el maestro de Armand, hasta su encuentro con Akasha y Enkil y su precipitada partida hacia "el nuevo mundo". <br />Sin dudas, la historia es una de las más completas fuera de las crónicas individuales que anne rice publicó luego de "Memnoch, el demonio", y también una de las más interesantes y menos forzadas, ya que la narración fluye con naturalidad. <br />Para este momento, anne rice me tenía completamente "en sus manos", fua a partir de este punto que comencé a leer sus libros sin parar, tanto así, que sólo leí sus libros durante los siguientes meses. <br />Las tres primeras crónicas vampíricas siempre estaban a la mano en mi habitación. Lamentablemente, allí quedaron, en mi habitación en Buenos Aires por que al mudarme a México, tuve que ser algo selectiva con los libros que pude traer.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17711488072560428022">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11539752747905174864">A few random thoughts because I won't be reviewing this on my website: <br /><br />1. Simon Vance is a fantastic narrator. <br />2. I forgot how sensual Rice's writing is. Not "sexy" but overloaded with sensation. Lestat is a very emotional person who is captivated by sensation and prone to love easily. Rice really infuses her book with that. It's quite astonishing.<br />3. I absolutely loved how she wove history and myth into it all.<br />4. Vampires are dark, as they should be. <br />5. Some parts of the novel were a bit too dra</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11539752747905174864">A few random thoughts because I won't be reviewing this on my website: <br /><br />1. Simon Vance is a fantastic narrator. <br />2. I forgot how sensual Rice's writing is. Not "sexy" but overloaded with sensation. Lestat is a very emotional person who is captivated by sensation and prone to love easily. Rice really infuses her book with that. It's quite astonishing.<br />3. I absolutely loved how she wove history and myth into it all.<br />4. Vampires are dark, as they should be. <br />5. Some parts of the novel were a bit too drawn out. </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_97812295">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/97812295" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1465483-mochacocafan" class="left imgcol" title="Mochacocafan"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1219795858p2/1465483.jpg" alt="Mochacocafan" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/97812295?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 09, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1465483-mochacocafan" class="user" title="Mochacocafan">Mochacocafan</a>

          added it


          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/386376.The_Vampire_Lestat" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345313867" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer97812295">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3680713806741645392">Let me clear one thing up: I haven't read <em>Queen of the Damned</em> yet, but this book definitely increased my love for Lestat.<br /><br />In <em>Interview With the Vampire</em>, Lestat read to me as the aristocratic, realistic, practical vampire with a lust for blood and opinions grounded in blunt reality. I liked him as a villain, and I love him as a hero. Louis felt to me like a melodramatic teenager with a flair for angsty sololiquies. I don't hate him, but I don't have a passion for his character.<br /><br />Lestat's history is</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3680713806741645392">Let me clear one thing up: I haven't read <em>Queen of the Damned</em> yet, but this book definitely increased my love for Lestat.<br /><br />In <em>Interview With the Vampire</em>, Lestat read to me as the aristocratic, realistic, practical vampire with a lust for blood and opinions grounded in blunt reality. I liked him as a villain, and I love him as a hero. Louis felt to me like a melodramatic teenager with a flair for angsty sololiquies. I don't hate him, but I don't have a passion for his character.<br /><br />Lestat's history is mildly disturbing, especially his flip-flopping love for his mother, but he does have flaws and personality, and that makes him interesting. He's the charming, gorgeous young man who will drink your blood, slay evildoers, play the piano, argue intelligently with a sophisticated French accent, and love his fellow vampires and mortals in a darkly honest way I love.<br /><br />Lestat is the neo-European vampire, graceful and deadly. Yes, his O.O Claudia incident was a mistake, but hey, no-one is perfect. And this golden-haired vampire does come close.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3680713806741645392">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_173917296">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/173917296" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5565767-monika" class="left imgcol" title="Monika"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="Monika" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/173917296?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 05, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5565767-monika" class="user" title="Monika">Monika</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/43814.The_Vampire_Lestat" title="Paperback 9780345476883" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5565767-monika?shelf=unforgettable" class="actionLinkLite">unforgettable</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5565767-monika?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5565767-monika?shelf=vampires" class="actionLinkLite">vampires</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5565767-monika?shelf=journey-across-the-world" class="actionLinkLite">journey-across-the-world</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5565767-monika?shelf=single-hero-stuff" class="actionLinkLite">single-hero-stuff</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer173917296">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13578295995377994134">I was somewhere between middle and high school, and craved for something dark. I've never read "The Interview", but seen the movie, so when I found a shelf in bookstore with Rice on it, I immediately reached for Lestat as the second in the series. <br />And it comepletely blowed my mind back then. I remember marvelling on how <em>real</em> and <em>alive</em> the characters felt to me. I couldn't believe that all that was a product of imagination of one person. I loved the richness of Lestat's character, with all its fl</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13578295995377994134">I was somewhere between middle and high school, and craved for something dark. I've never read "The Interview", but seen the movie, so when I found a shelf in bookstore with Rice on it, I immediately reached for Lestat as the second in the series. <br />And it comepletely blowed my mind back then. I remember marvelling on how <em>real</em> and <em>alive</em> the characters felt to me. I couldn't believe that all that was a product of imagination of one person. I loved the richness of Lestat's character, with all its flaws, loved Marcus's background story, and how everything else was so logical, so believable. When I finally put down the book, I was nearly convinced such creatures really existed out there somewhere. Ii was amazing.<br /><br />As I said, it was years ago, but that's how I remember this book and I couldn't give it less than five stars. Maybe, if I've read it now, I'd have different opinion on it. But one thing I know is true even now. Lestat was the first vampire I've read about and formed my idea about them. With today's vampire-themed-book overflow, that's something I deeply appreciate.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13578295995377994134">...more</a>

          </span>

      <a href="/user/show/7475930-amber" class="user" title="Amber">Amber</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer264642150">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3321050425930519617">I really enjoyed this novel and was so drawn in by the mind of Lestat. It took me awhile to pick this up after reading "Interview W/ The Vampire" because I felt like Louis was so depressing and I needed a break after reading it. Lestat is so much more charming and his life contains far more intrigue than his American counterparts. This novel cast Lestat in a completely different light, and really shows you just how ridiculous Louis &amp; Claudia may have been being. (Saw that coming, total drama</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3321050425930519617">I really enjoyed this novel and was so drawn in by the mind of Lestat. It took me awhile to pick this up after reading "Interview W/ The Vampire" because I felt like Louis was so depressing and I needed a break after reading it. Lestat is so much more charming and his life contains far more intrigue than his American counterparts. This novel cast Lestat in a completely different light, and really shows you just how ridiculous Louis &amp; Claudia may have been being. (Saw that coming, total drama queens) I completely fell in love with Gabriel, and wish Anne had written a novel dedicated to the telling of her story! I honestly couldn't put this book down, it was pretty long, but all of it is good. I love Anne Rice's language, and her skill with it is evident in this novel. If you like quotes keep your highlighter handy.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1807268923891209430">This story was told by the same guy who had read the audiobook for The Gunslinger by Stephen King. It was a really good narration he really puts you into the mind of Lestat. A tale of the coming of age/vampire of Lestat, you are taken through different timelines of his life through centuries. It was a very deep memoir of his, Anne rice really knows how to use words elegantly in this story. There were times that the life story became a bore and felt like he was self loathing. It brings me back to</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1807268923891209430">This story was told by the same guy who had read the audiobook for The Gunslinger by Stephen King. It was a really good narration he really puts you into the mind of Lestat. A tale of the coming of age/vampire of Lestat, you are taken through different timelines of his life through centuries. It was a very deep memoir of his, Anne rice really knows how to use words elegantly in this story. There were times that the life story became a bore and felt like he was self loathing. It brings me back to the Dexter books and his insight as a killer and all his dark passenger rambles. I enjoyed the first book Interview with a vampire more.</span>
