<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_991347779">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/991347779" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/6368180-rachelvlehcar" class="left imgcol" title="RachelvlehcaR"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1417324228p2/6368180.jpg" alt="RachelvlehcaR" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/991347779?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 18, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6368180-rachelvlehcar" class="user" title="RachelvlehcaR">RachelvlehcaR</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6989932-the-vampire-lestat" title="Paperback " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/6368180-rachelvlehcar?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6368180-rachelvlehcar?shelf=horror" class="actionLinkLite">horror</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6368180-rachelvlehcar?shelf=paranormal" class="actionLinkLite">paranormal</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6368180-rachelvlehcar?shelf=10-series-to-read-or-read" class="actionLinkLite">10-series-to-read-or-read</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6368180-rachelvlehcar?shelf=14-chunky-book-challenge" class="actionLinkLite">14-chunky-book-challenge</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6368180-rachelvlehcar?shelf=favorites-read-2015" class="actionLinkLite">favorites-read-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer991347779">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14208200754594888709">I read this when in middle school. Interview with the Vampire was my first grown up book. I read it in 7th grade, thanks to my cousin that said I must read this series. At the time there was only three books. <a title="Interview with the Vampire (The Vampire Chronicles, #1) by Anne Rice" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43763.Interview_with_the_Vampire__The_Vampire_Chronicles___1_">Interview with the Vampire</a>, <a title="The Vampire Lestat (The Vampire Chronicles, #2) by Anne Rice" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43814.The_Vampire_Lestat__The_Vampire_Chronicles___2_">The Vampire Lestat</a>, and <a title="The Queen of the Damned (The Vampire Chronicles, #3) by Anne Rice" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43758.The_Queen_of_the_Damned__The_Vampire_Chronicles___3_">The Queen of the Damned</a><br /><br />I read this and loved it more than Interview with the Vampire. It is a book about Lestat, his maker, and those around him. It's a tragic story and makes you question so many things. At least it did for me when I read</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14208200754594888709">I read this when in middle school. Interview with the Vampire was my first grown up book. I read it in 7th grade, thanks to my cousin that said I must read this series. At the time there was only three books. <a title="Interview with the Vampire (The Vampire Chronicles, #1) by Anne Rice" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43763.Interview_with_the_Vampire__The_Vampire_Chronicles___1_">Interview with the Vampire</a>, <a title="The Vampire Lestat (The Vampire Chronicles, #2) by Anne Rice" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43814.The_Vampire_Lestat__The_Vampire_Chronicles___2_">The Vampire Lestat</a>, and <a title="The Queen of the Damned (The Vampire Chronicles, #3) by Anne Rice" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43758.The_Queen_of_the_Damned__The_Vampire_Chronicles___3_">The Queen of the Damned</a><br /><br />I read this and loved it more than Interview with the Vampire. It is a book about Lestat, his maker, and those around him. It's a tragic story and makes you question so many things. At least it did for me when I read it the first time. I called it my little red bible. This was back in 1990 and 1991 before the whole sparkling vampire craze.<br /><br />It built the Anne Rice world of Vampires which boomed. I'm very embarrassed about the movies but imagining they never have been made makes my world a better place--even if the soundtrack is great. This series and book made me jump into everything Anne Rice. I became a huge fan and read all her books while in high school--including <a title="The Mummy, or Ramses the Damned by Anne Rice" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1183696.The_Mummy__or_Ramses_the_Damned">The Mummy, or Ramses the Damned</a> (Which will never be finished--this is before the internet). There is a lot of name dropping of Ramses in this book. This is also what made me pick up The Mummy.<br /><br />This re-read took me back to that time in my life and a lot of the topics and thoughts from the book that I wasn't able to fully understand then. I remembered a lot but also forgot a huge amount.<br /><br />This is a must read. Same with the other series (Mayfair Witches) I loved of hers--<a title="The Witching Hour (Lives of the Mayfair Witches, #1) by Anne Rice" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11901.The_Witching_Hour__Lives_of_the_Mayfair_Witches___1_">The Witching Hour</a>! Now I want to read all my Anne Rice books.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14208200754594888709">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_79066010">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/79066010" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2806902-chipper" class="left imgcol" title="Chipper"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1254724985p2/2806902.jpg" alt="Chipper" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/79066010?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 26, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2806902-chipper" class="user" title="Chipper">Chipper</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/43814.The_Vampire_Lestat" title="Paperback 9780345476883" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer79066010">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3669741648655593793">After thoroughly enjoying Rice's Interview With the Vampire, I fully expected to be let down by her second installment in The Vampire Chronicles: The Vampire Lestat. I was not. The Vampire Lestat is a fascinating character and novel. Like its predecessor, this novel is not a pop-culture vampire tale crafted for teenagers. Rather, it explores the problems, complications and inner-strife that immortality gives rise to and the larger questions an immortal might ask and seek to discover in himself,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3669741648655593793">After thoroughly enjoying Rice's Interview With the Vampire, I fully expected to be let down by her second installment in The Vampire Chronicles: The Vampire Lestat. I was not. The Vampire Lestat is a fascinating character and novel. Like its predecessor, this novel is not a pop-culture vampire tale crafted for teenagers. Rather, it explores the problems, complications and inner-strife that immortality gives rise to and the larger questions an immortal might ask and seek to discover in himself, his peers and his ancestors.<br /><br />Although a sequel to Interview With the Vampire, The Vampire Lestat chronicles through the ages the life of Lestat de Lioncourt, providing a great deal of depth to a character readers/movie goers may have thought they understood during Interview With the Vampire. In my experience, never has a character and his experiences been so underestimated, so different than what a reader should have expected based on a preceding novel.<br /><br />It should not be overlooked that much of the relevant history of Rice's vampire world is explained and I found the characters and historical backdrop, particularly the stories told by Marius, mesmerizing, and a perfect set up for the third installment of The Vampire Chronicles: Queen of the Damned. Can't wait to see where this goes ...<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3669741648655593793">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_527092208">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/527092208" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4585123-misal" class="left imgcol" title="Misal"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1404611019p2/4585123.jpg" alt="Misal" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/527092208?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 01, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4585123-misal" class="user" title="Misal">Misal</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/70988.The_Vampire_Lestat" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780708831533" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4585123-misal?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4585123-misal?shelf=read-in-2013" class="actionLinkLite">read-in-2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer527092208">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14189040211536349823">(WHAT THE HELL GOODREADS WHY DID YOU DELETE MY REVIEW???) <br /><br />As someone who loves vampires, I've had the misfortune of never reading any decent literature concerning them thus far. There was the dreaded <em>Twilight</em> series, and the marginally better <em>Blue Bloods</em> series (well, the first two books, really), and I never even got past the first couple of pages of <em>Dead Until Dark</em> before tossing it aside. None of these were exactly what you'd refer to as gems of vampire literature.<br /><br />But then one day my friend h</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14189040211536349823">(WHAT THE HELL GOODREADS WHY DID YOU DELETE MY REVIEW???) <br /><br />As someone who loves vampires, I've had the misfortune of never reading any decent literature concerning them thus far. There was the dreaded <em>Twilight</em> series, and the marginally better <em>Blue Bloods</em> series (well, the first two books, really), and I never even got past the first couple of pages of <em>Dead Until Dark</em> before tossing it aside. None of these were exactly what you'd refer to as gems of vampire literature.<br /><br />But then one day my friend hands me this books and tells me I <em>have</em> to read it, forget the fact that I haven't read <em>Interview With a Vampire</em> before. So I start this book, mildly curious and spurred on by my rekindled love for vampires with my Buffy rewatch. Immediately, I end up thinking it's some kind of joke because when we are introduced to Lestat, he is about to become a rockstar and I found myself thinking 'how is a rockstar vampire any better than a vampire who sparkles in the sun?'<br /><br />Turns out, I was wrong. Lestat was <em>much</em> better than a sparkly vampire. This book was full of interesting characters (I loved almost everyone we were introduced to), had wonderfully sensuous prose, and a plot that was engaging and relatively fast paced considering its length.<br /><br />But the real reason this book gets five stars? <br /><br />Lestat. <br /><br />God, I <em>love</em> him. He's a rebel, but a sensitive rebel, and not sensitive in a way that often comes off as annoying. He cares for the pleasures of mortal life even after being changed, longs for companionship and I'm pretty sure he's described feeling an inexplicably strong love for every single character he meets from Nicholas to Marius (even Akasha, I think?) It's <em>adorable</em> (excuse my cooing). I haven't read <em>Interview...</em>, or seen the move but judging him from just what we've seen in this book, Lestat is one of the most entertaining protagonists I've read in a while and is definitely going down in my list of favorite male literary characters. <br /><br />And the whole Rockstar thing? Hilariously fitting and pretty well executed when taken into context. <br /><br />I cannot do justice to this book in a review, it's difficult to explain just how brilliantly Anne Rice threads the plot together and makes her characters likable, and if not that then at least relatable, and <em>alive</em> despite their being technically dead. You keep wanting to revisit this world, and I think whenever I come back to re-read this book, it will be just as thrilling and enriching an experience as it was this time around. <br /><br />For now, I'm looking forward to reading more of this series. Still trying to decide if I should go back and read <em>Interview...</em> or proceed with <em>Queen of the Damned</em>.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14189040211536349823">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_48874868">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/48874868" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2115855-lindsay-wing" class="left imgcol" title="Lindsay Wing"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1236743838p2/2115855.jpg" alt="Lindsay Wing" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/48874868?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 14, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2115855-lindsay-wing" class="user" title="Lindsay Wing">Lindsay Wing</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/43814.The_Vampire_Lestat" title="Paperback 9780345476883" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2115855-lindsay-wing?shelf=best-books-ever" class="actionLinkLite">best-books-ever</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer48874868">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11808763409382198445">Obviously, as a tormented, emo teenager, I was way obsessed with this book, and I remembered that a lot of that was based in the fact that I was an angsty 14-year-old. Now, years later, I decided to re-read it for kicks and I have to say that it's still fantastic, and that assertion is in no way based in any stupid self-indulgent fascination with suffering. It's just a beautifully written book. It starts off slow, but the second half is striking and magnificently written. Rice uses some of the m</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11808763409382198445">Obviously, as a tormented, emo teenager, I was way obsessed with this book, and I remembered that a lot of that was based in the fact that I was an angsty 14-year-old. Now, years later, I decided to re-read it for kicks and I have to say that it's still fantastic, and that assertion is in no way based in any stupid self-indulgent fascination with suffering. It's just a beautifully written book. It starts off slow, but the second half is striking and magnificently written. Rice uses some of the most poetic language I've ever read and even though the subject matter is a little bit trite ("oh it's so sexy to be a vampire, yadda, yadda, yadda"), Rice has a particular talent for crafting characters that are fascinating in their psychological acceptance of their un-dead lifestyle, and whose perception of the world around them, as immortals, sheds a fantastically beautiful rendering of our lives as "mortals." This book makes me want to discover the beauty in my own life and experience and to embrace fully the supernatural elegance and grace of our immortal planet and our undying humanity.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11808763409382198445">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('j6cT/S3XB8QDJcGWMCZAvsoV3SQB55tFsHR53yCQbcTqcywu3wUTPo/9tS1OR6YMg+IePUg63O/afXxN7AWbgQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gayXDO0VYjosniHmpGFkToBNr5/vHFBiXrrgkEq9v0zkeKjfH8d2wKBGVV3aAIL8ybpshqbBF8g0s+UChihJCQ==')})
  }

The Talc of the Body Thief Memnoch the Devil. With her bestselling, epic saga, Anne Rice has reinvented the legend and literature of one of fiction\'s most popular and captivating archetypes. Now, Katherine Ramsland, Anne Rice\'s biographer, has completely revised and updated the ultimate reference guide to the world, history, and adventures of these haunting characters, from the unforgettable Lestat to Rice\'s newest chilling creation, Memnoch the Devil.Written with the full cooperation of Anne Rice -- and now with more than 1,200 entries -- The Vampire Companion offers an insightful exploration, appreciation, and interpretation of all the characters and events, names and places, symbols and themes in the five volumes of The Vampire Chronicles, including more than one hundred pages of new entries on Rice\'s latest vampire novel, Memnoch the Devil. Everything that readers might want to explore further is annotated and analyzed in this entertaining and enlightening work: the unforgettable characters of Louis, Lestat, Claudia, Akasha, Armand, and Memnoch; the important points of interest on Lestat\'s fascinating tour through Heaven and Hell; ancient lore; Rice\'s unique contributions to the mythos of vampires; the literary inspirations that echo through the novels; Rice\'s own reflections and revelations about her work and about the movie Interview with the Vampire; and much more.Richly illustrated with new photos, drawings, maps, and a complete time line of events in The Chronicles, The Vampire Companion is as captivating as the phenomenal saga it explores.     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/7577.Anne_Rice">About Anne Rice</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/7577.Anne_Rice"><img alt="7577" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1383250078p2/7577.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer14775450095823593362">Anne Rice (born Howard Allen Frances O'Brien) is a best-selling American author of gothic, supernatural, historical, erotica, and later religious themed books. Best known for <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/search?utf8=%E2%9C%93&amp;query=The+Vampire+Chronicles">The Vampire Chronicles</a>, her prevailing thematical focus is on love, death, immortality, existentialism, and the human condition. She was married to poet <a title="Stan Rice" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/222961.Stan_Rice">Stan Rice</a> for 41 years until his death in 2002. Her books have sold near</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14775450095823593362">Anne Rice (born Howard Allen Frances O'Brien) is a best-selling American author of gothic, supernatural, historical, erotica, and later religious themed books. Best known for <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/search?utf8=%E2%9C%93&amp;query=The+Vampire+Chronicles">The Vampire Chronicles</a>, her prevailing thematical focus is on love, death, immortality, existentialism, and the human condition. She was married to poet <a title="Stan Rice" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/222961.Stan_Rice">Stan Rice</a> for 41 years until his death in 2002. Her books have sold nearly 100 million copies, making her one of the most widely read authors in modern history.<br /><br />She uses the pseudonym <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/author/show/17553.Anne_Rampling">Anne Rampling</a> for adult-themed fiction (i.e., erotica) and <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/author/show/437669.A_N_Roquelaure">A.N. Roquelaure</a> for fiction featuring sexually explicit sado-masochism.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14775450095823593362">...more</a>

    </div>
    <a href="/author/show/7577.Anne_Rice" class="actionLink moreLink">More about Anne Rice...</a>
<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>

in a feat of mesmeric storytelling, a chillingly hypnotic entertainment in which the oldest and most powerful forces of the night are unleashed on an unsuspecting world.Three brilliantly colored narrative threads intertwine as the story unfolds:- The rock star known as Vampire Lestat, worshipped by millions of spellbound fans, prepares for a concert in San Francisco.  Among the audience--pilgrims in a blind swoon of adoration--are hundreds of vampires, creatures who see Lestat as a &amp;quot;greedy fiend risking the secret prosperity of all his kind just to be loved and seen by mortals,&amp;quot; fiends themselves who hate Lestat\'s power and who are determined to destroy him . . . - The sleep of certain men and women--vampires and mortals scattered around the world--is haunted by a vivid, mysterious dream: of twins with fiery red hair and piercing green eyes who suffer an unspeakable tragedy.  It is a dream that slowly, tauntingly reveals its meaning to the dreamers as they make their way toward each other--some to be destroyed on the journey, some to face an even more terrifying fate at journey\'s end . . . - Akasha--Queen of the Damned, mother of all vampires, rises after a 6,000 year sleep and puts into motion a heinous plan to &amp;quot;save&amp;quot; mankind from itself and make &amp;quot;all myths of the world real&amp;quot; by elevating herself and her chosen son/lover to the level of the gods: &amp;quot;I am the fulfillment and I shall from this moment be the cause&amp;quot; . . . These narrative threads wind sinuously across a vast, richly detailed tapestry of the violent, sensual world of vampirism, taking us back 6,000 years to its beginnings.  As the stories of the &amp;quot;first brood&amp;quot; of blood drinkers are revealed, we are swept across the ages, from Egypt to South America to the Himalayas to all the shrouded corners of the globe where vampires have left their mark. Vampires are created--mortals succumbing to the sensation of &amp;quot;being enptied, of being devoured, of being nothing.&amp;quot; Vampires are destroyed.  Dark rituals are performed--the rituals of ancient creatures prowling the modern world.  And, finally, we are brought to a moment in the twentieth century when, in an astonishing climax, the fate of the living dead--and perhaps of the living,
